interpret all that we in we unbelief call terrible in the utterance of torrent and storm as only varied expression of god 's eternal love chapter xiv the wild sheep -lrb- _ ovi montana _ -rrb- the wild sheep rank highest among the animal mountaineer of the sierra possess of keen sight and scent and strong limb he dwell secure amid the loftiest summit leap unscathed from crag to crag up and down the front of giddy precipice cross foam torrent and slope of frozen snow expose to the wildest storm yet maintain a brave warm life and develop from generation to generation in perfect strength and beauty nearly all the lofty mountain-chain of the globe be inhabit by wild sheep most of which on account of the remote and all but inaccessible region where they dwell be imperfectly know as yet they be classify by different naturalist under from five to ten distinct species or variety the best know be the burrhel of the himalaya -lrb- _ ovi burrhel _ blyth -rrb- the argalus the large wild sheep of central and northeastern asia -lrb- _ o ammon _ linn or _ caprovis argali _ -rrb- the corsican mouflon -lrb- _ o musimon _ pal -rrb- the aoudad of the mountain of northern africa -lrb- _ ammotragus tragelaphus _ -rrb- and the rocky mountain bighorn -lrb- _ o montana _ cuv -rrb- to this last-named species belong the wild sheep of the sierra its range accord to the late professor baird of the smithsonian institution extend from the region of the upper missourus and yellowstone to the rocky mountain and the high grounds adjacent to they on the eastern slope and as far south as the rio grande westward it extend to the coast range of washington oregon and californium and follow the highland some distance into mexico -lrb- 1 -rrb- throughout the vast region bound on the east by the wahsatch mountain and on the west by the sierra there be more than a hundred subordinate range and mountain group trend north and south range beyond range with summit rise from eight to twelve thousand foot above the level of the sea probably all of which accord to my own observation be or have be inhabit by this species compare with the argalus which consider its size and the vast extent of its range be probably the most important of all the wild sheep we species be about the same size but the horn be less twisted and less divergent the more important characteristic be however essentially the same some of the best naturalist maintain that the two be only varied form of one species in accordance with this view cuvier conjecture that since central asia seem to be the region where the sheep first appear and from which it have be distribute the argalus may have be distribute over this continent from asia by cross ber strait on ice this conjecture be not so ill found as at on its wing be scarcely perceptible the bird be assemble beneath leafy shade or make short languid flight in search of food all save the majestic buzzard with broad wing outspread he sail the warm air unwearily from ridge to ridge seem to enjoy the fervid sunshine like a butterfly squirrel too whose spicy ardor no heat or cold may abate be nutting among the pine and the innumerable host of the insect kingdom be throb and waver unwearied as sunbeam this brushy berry-bearing region use to be a deer and bear pasture but since the disturbance of the gold period these fine animal have almost wholly disappear here also once roam the mastodon and elephant whose bone be find entomb in the river gravel and beneath thick fold of lava toward noon as we be ride slowly over bank and bra basking in the unfeverish sun-heat we witness the upheaval of a new mountain-range a sierra of cloud abound in landscape as truly sublime and beautiful -- if only we have a mind to think so and eye to see -- as the more ancient rocky sierra beneath it with its forest and waterfall remind we that as there be a lower world of cave so also there be a upper world of cloud huge bossy cumulus develop with astonishing rapidity from mere bud swell with visible motion into colossal mountain and pile higher higher in long massive range peak beyond peak dome over dome with many a picturesque valley and shadowy cave between while the dark fir and pine of the upper bench of the sierra be project against they pearl boss with exquisite clearness of outline these cloud mountain vanish in the azure as quickly as they be develop leave no detritus but they be not a whit less real or interesting on this account the more enduring hill over which we ride be vanish as surely as they only not so fast a difference which be great or small accord to the standpoint from which it be contemplate at the bottom of every dell we find little homestead embosome in wild brush and vine wherever the recession of the hill leave patch of arable ground these secluded flat be settle mostly by italian and german who plant a few vegetable and grape-vine at odd time while they main business be mine and prospect in spite of all the natural beauty of these dell cabin they can hardly be call home they be only a better kind of camp gladly abandon whenever the hoped-for gold harvest have be gather there be a air of profound unrest and melancholy about the best of they they beauty be thrust upon they by exuberant nature apart from which they be only a few log and board rudely joint and without either ceiling or indicate the trend of they owner ' hard life the ride from murphy 's to the cave be scarcely two hour long but we linger among quartz-ledge and bank of dead river gravel until long after noon at length emerge from a narrow-throated gorge a small house come in sight set in a thicket of fig-tree at the base of a limestone hill that say my guide point to the house be cave city and the cave be in that gray hill arrive at the one house of this one-house city we be boisterously welcome by three drunken man who have come to town to hold a spree the mistress of the house try to keep order and in reply to we inquiry tell we that the cave guide be then in the cave with a party of lady and must we wait until he return we ask no that be unnecessary we might take candle and go into the cave alone provide we shout from time to time so as to be find by the guide and be careful not to fall over the rock or into the dark pool accordingly take a trail from the house we be lead around the base of the hill to the mouth of the cave a small inconspicuous archway mossy around the edge and shape like the door of a water-ouzel 's nest with no appreciable hint or advertisement of the grandeur of the many crystal chamber within light we candle which seem to have no illuminating power in the thick darkness we grope we way onward as best we could along narrow lane and alley from chamber to chamber sparkling crystal some of the corridor be muddy and in plod along these we seem to be in the street of some prairie village in spring-time then we would come to handsome marble stairway conduct right ah it be nice it be splendid they all reply and echo the bridal chamber back here be just glorious this morning we come down from the calaveras big tree grove and the tree be nothing to it after make italian lead we into the heart of the hill up and down right and left from chamber to chamber more and more magnificent all a-glitter like a glacier cave with icicle-like stalactite and stalagmite where a priest have say mass mass-saying be not so generally develop in connection with natural wonder as dance one of the first conceit excite by the giant sequoia be to cut one of they down and inaccessible south dome would likely follow the making of a easy way to the top of it it be delightful to witness here the infinite deliberation of nature and the simplicity of she method in the production of such mighty result such perfect repose combine with restless enthusiastic energy though cold and bloodless as a landscape of polar ice building be go on in the dark with incessant activity the archway and ceiling be everywhere hang with down-growing crystal like inverted grove of leafless sapling some of they large other delicately attenuate each tip with a single drop of water like the terminal bud of a pine-tree the only appreciable sound be the drip and tinkle of water fail into pool or faintly plash on the crystal floor in some place the crystal decoration be arrange in graceful flow fold deeply plicate like stiff silken drapery in other straight line of the ordinary stalactite form be combine with reference to size and tone in a regularly graduate system like the string of a harp with musical tone correspond thereto and on these stone harp we play by strike the crystal string with a stick the delicious liquid tone they give forth seem perfectly divine as they sweetly whisper and waver through the majestic hall and die away in faintest cadence -- the music of fairy-land here we linger and revel rejoice to find so much music in stony silence so much splendor in darkness so many mansion in the depths of the mountain building ever in process of construction yet ever finish develop from perfection to perfection profusion without overabundance every particle visible or invisible in glorious motion march to the music of the sphere in a region regard as the abode of eternal stillness and death the outer chamber of mountain cave be frequently select as home by wild beast in the sierra however they seem to prefer home and hiding-place in chaparral and beneath shelve precipice as i have never see they track in any of the cave this be the more remarkable we feel we faith in nature 's beauty strengthen and see more clearly that beauty be universal and immortal above beneath on land and sea mountain and plain in heat and cold light and darkness chapter xvi the bee-pasture when californium be wild it be one sweet bee-garden throughout its entire length north and south and all the way across from the snowy sierra to the ocean wherever a bee might fly within the bound of this virgin wilderness -- through the redwood forest along the bank of the river along the bluff and headland front the sea over valley and plain park and grove and deep leafy glen or far up the piny slope of the mountain -- throughout every belt and section of climate up to the timber line bee-flower bloom in lavish abundance here they grow more or less apart in special sheet and patch of no great size there in broad flow fold hundred of mile in length -- zone of polleny forest zone of flowery chaparral stream-tangle of rubus and wild rise sheet of golden composite bed of violet bed of mint bed of bryanthus and clover and so on certain species bloom somewhere all the year round but of late year plow and sheep have make sad havoc in these glorious pasture destroy ten of thousand of the flowery acre like a fire and banish many species of the best honey-plant to rocky cliff and fence-corner while on the other hand cultivation thus far have give no adequate compensation at least in kind only acre of alfalfa for mile of the richest wild pasture ornamental rose and honeysuckle around cottage door for cascade of wild rose in the dell and small square orchard and orange-grove for broad mountain-belt of chaparral the great central plain of californium during the month of march April and may be one smooth continuous bed of honey-bloom so marvelously rich that in walk from one end of it to the other a distance of more than 400 mile you foot would press about a hundred flower at every step mint gilias nemophila castilleia and innumerable composita be so crowd together that have ninety-nine per cent of they be take away the plain would still have seem to any but californian extravagantly flowery the radiant honeyful corolla touch and overlap and rise above one another glow in the living light like a sunset sky -- one sheet of purple and gold with the bright sacramento pour through the midst of it from the north the san joaquin from the south and they many tributary sweep in at right angle from the mountain divide the plain into section fringe with tree along the river there be a strip of bottom-land countersunk beneath the general level and wider toward the foot-hill where magnificent oak from three to eight foot in diameter cast grateful mass of shade over the open prairie-like level and close along the water 's edge there be a fine jungle of tropical luxuriance compose of wild-rose and bramble bush and a great variety of climb vine wreathe and interlace the branch and trunk of willow and alder and swing across from summit to summit in heavy festoon here the wild bee revel in fresh bloom long after the flower of the drier plain have wither and go to seed and in midsummer when the blackberry be ripe the indian come from the mountain to feast -- man woman and baby in long noisy train often join by the farmer of the neighborhood who gather this wild fruit with commendable appreciation of its superior flavor while they home orchard be full of ripe peach apricot nectarine and fig and they vineyard be laden with grape but though these luxuriant shaggy river-bed be thus distinct from the smooth treeless plain they make no heavy divide line in general view the whole appear as one continuous sheet of bloom bound only by the mountain when i first saw this central garden the most extensive and regular of all the bee-pasture of the state it seem all one sheet of plant gold hazy and vanish in the distance distinct as a new map along the foot-hill at my foot descend the eastern slope of the coast range through bed of gilia and lupine and around many a breezy hillock and bush-crowned headland i at length wade out into the midst of it all the ground be cover not with grass and green leaf but with radiant corolla about ankle-deep next the foot-hill knee-deep or more five or six mile out here be bahium madium madarium burrielium chrysopsis corethrogyne grindelium etc grow in close social congregation of various shades of yellow blending finely with the purple of clarkium orthocarpus and oenothera whose delicate petal be drink the vital sunbeam without give back any sparkling glow -lrb- illustration : a bee-ranch in lower californium -rrb- because so long a period of extreme drought succeed the rainy season most of the vegetation be compose of annual which spring up simultaneously and bloom together at about the same height above the ground the general surface be but slightly ruffle by the taller phacelia pentstemon and group of _ salvia carduacea _ the king of the mint saunter in any direction hundred of these happy sun-plant brush against my foot at every step and close over they as if i be wade in liquid gold the air be sweet with fragrance the lark sing they bless song rise on the wing as i advance then sink out of sight in the polleny sod while myriad of wild bee stir the lower air with they monotonous hum -- monotonous yet forever fresh and sweet as every-day sunshine hare and spermophile show themselves in considerable number in shallow place and small band of antelope be almost constantly in sight gaze curiously from some slight elevation and then bound swiftly away with unrivaled grace of motion yet i could discover no crushed flower to mark they track nor indeed any destructive action of any wild foot or tooth whatever the great yellow day circle by uncounted while i drift toward the north observe the countless form of life throng about I lie down almost anywhere on the approach of night and what glorious botanical bed i have oftentimes on awake i would find several new species lean over I and look I full in the face so that my study would begin before rise about the first of may i turn eastward cross the san joaquin river between the mouth of the tuolumne and merce and by the time i have reach the sierra foot-hill most of the vegetation have go to seed and become as dry as hay all the season of the great plain be warm or temperate and bee-flower be never wholly want but the grand springtime -- the annual resurrection -- be govern by the rain which usually set in about the middle of November or the beginning of December then the seed that for six month have lie on the ground dry and fresh as if they have be gather into barn at once unfold they treasured life the general brown and purple of the ground and the dead vegetation of the preceding year give place to the green of moss and liverwort and myriad of young leaf then one species after another come into flower gradually overspread the green with yellow and purple which last until may the rainy season be by no mean a gloomy soggy period of constant cloudiness and rain perhaps nowhere else in north america perhaps in the world be the month of December January February and march so full of bland plant-building sunshine refer to my note of the winter and spring of 1868-69 every day of which i spend out of door on that section of the plain lie between the tuolumne and merce river i find that the first rain of the season fall on December 18th January have only six rainy day -- that be day on which rain fall February three march five April three and may three complete the so-called rainy season which be about a average one the ordinary rain-storm of this region be seldom very cold or violent the wind which in settle weather come from the northwest veer round into the opposite direction the sky fill gradually and evenly with one general cloud from which the rain fall steadily often for day in succession at a temperature of about 45 ° or 50 ° more than seventy-five per cent of all the rain of this season come from the northwest down the coast over southeastern alaska british columbium washington and oregon though the local wind of these circular storm blow from the southeast one magnificent local storm from the northwest fall on march 21 a massive round-browed cloud come swell and thunder over the flowery plain in most impose majesty its bossy front burning white and purple in the full blaze of the sun while warm rain pour from its ample fountain like a cataract beat down flower and bee and flood the dry watercourse as suddenly as those of nevada be flood by the so-called cloudburst but in less than half a hour not a trace of the heavy mountain-like cloud-structure be leave in the sky and the bee be on the wing as if nothing more gratefully refresh could have be send they by the end of January four species of plant be in flower and five or six moss have already adjust they hood and be in the prime of life but the flower be not sufficiently numerous as yet to affect greatly the general green of the young leaf violet make they appearance in the first week of February and toward the end of this month the warmer portion of the plain be already golden with myriad of the flower of rayed composite this be the full springtime the sunshine grow warmer and richer new plant bloom every day the air become more tuneful with hum wing and sweeter with the fragrance of the opening flower ant and ground squirrel be get ready for they summer work rub they benumbed limb and sun themselves on the husk-pile before they door and spider be busy mend they old web or weave new one in march the vegetation be more than double in depth and color claytonium calandrinium a large white gilium and two nemophila be in bloom together with a host of yellow composite tall enough now to bend in the wind and show waver ripple of shade in April plant-life as a whole reach its greatest height and the plain over all its varied surface be mantle with a close furred plush of purple and golden corolla by the end of this month most of the species have ripen they seed but undecayed still seem to be in bloom from the numerous corolla-like involucre and whorl of chaffy scale of the composite in may the bee find in flower only a few deep-set liliaceous plant and eriogonum June July August and September be the season of rest and sleep -- a winter of dry heat -- follow in October by a second outburst of bloom at the very driest time of the year then after the shrunken mass of leaf and stalk of the dead vegetation crinkle and turn to dust beneath the foot as if it have be baked in a oven _ hemizonium virga _ a slender unobtrusive little plant from six inch to three foot high suddenly make its appearance in patch mile in extent like a resurrection of the bloom of April i have count upward of 3000 flower five eighth of a inch in diameter on a single plant both its leaf and stem be so slender as to be nearly invisible at a distance of a few yard amid so showy a multitude of flower the ray and disk flower be both yellow the stamen purple and the texture of the ray be rich and velvety like the petal of garden pansy the prevailing wind turn all the head round to the southeast so that in face northwestward we have the flower look we in the face in my estimation this little plant the last bear of the brilliant host of composita that glorify the plain be the most interesting of all it remain in flower until November unite with two or three species of wiry eriogonum which continue the floral chain around December to the spring flower of January thus although the main bloom and honey season be only about three month long the floral circle however thin around some of the hot rainless month be never completely break how long the various species of wild bee have live in this honey-garden nobody know probably ever since the main body of the present flora gain possession of the land toward the close of the glacial period the first brown honey-bee bring to californium be say to have arrive in san francisco in march 1853 a bee-keeper by the name of shelton purchase a lot consist of twelve swarm from some one at aspinwall who have bring they from new york when land at san francisco all the hive contain live bee but they finally dwindle to one hive which be take to san josé the little immigrant flourish and multiply in the bountiful pasture of the santa clara valley send off three swarm the first season the owner be kill shortly afterward and in settle up he estate two of the swarm be sell at auction for $ 105 and $ 110 respectively other importation be make from time to time by way of the isthmus and though great pain be take to insure success about one half usually die on the way four swarm be bring safely across the plain in 1859 the hive be place in the rear end of a wagon which be stop in the afternoon to allow the bee to fly and feed in the floweriest place that be within reach until dark when the hive be close in 1855 two year after the time of the first arrival from new york a single swarm be bring over from san josé and let fly in the great central plain bee-culture however have never gain much attention here notwithstanding the extraordinary abundance of honey-bloom and the high price of honey during the early year a few hive be find here and there among settler who chance to have learn something about the business before come to the state but sheep cattle grain and fruit raising be the chief industry as they require less skill and care while the profit thus far have be greater in 1856 honey sell here at from one and a half to two dollar per pound twelve year later the price have fall to twelve and a half cent in 1868 i sit down to dinner with a band of ravenous sheep-shearer at a ranch on the san joaquin where fifteen or twenty hive be keep and we host advise we not to spare the large pan of honey he have place on the table as it be the cheapest article he have to offer in all my walk however i have never come upon a regular bee-ranch in the central valley like those so common and so skilfully manage in the southern county of the state the few pound of honey and wax produce be consume at home and be scarcely take into account among the coarser product of the farm the swarm that escape from they careless owner have a weary perplexing time of it in seek suitable home most of they make they way to the foot-hill of the mountain or to the tree that line the bank of the river where some hollow log or trunk may be find a friend of mine while out hunting on the san joaquin come upon a old coon trap hide among some tall grass near the edge of the river upon which he sit down to rest shortly afterward he attention be attract to a crowd of angry bee that be fly excitedly about he head when he discover that he be sit upon they hive which be find to contain more than 200 pound of honey out in the broad swampy delta of the sacramento and san joaquin river the little wanderer have be know to build they comb in a bunch of rush or stiff wiry grass only slightly protect from the weather and in danger every spring of be carry away by flood they have the advantage however of a vast extent of fresh pasture accessible only to themselves the present condition of the grand central garden be very different from that we have sketch about twenty year ago when the gold placer have be pretty thoroughly exhaust the attention of fortune-seeker -- not home-seeker -- be in great part turn away from the mine to the fertile plain and many begin experiment in a kind of restless wild agriculture a load of lumber would be haul to some spot on the free wilderness where water could be easily find and a rude box-cabin build then a gang-plow be procure and a dozen mustang pony worth ten or fifteen dollar apiece and with these hundred of acre be stir as easily as if the land have be under cultivation for year tough perennial root be almost wholly absent thus a ranch be establish and from these bare wooden hut as center of desolation the wild flora vanish in ever-widening circle but the arch destroyer be the shepherd with they flock of hoofed locust sweep over the ground like a fire and trample down every rod that escape the plow as completely as if the whole plain be a cottage garden-plot without a fence but notwithstanding these destroyer a thousand swarm of bee may be pasture here for every one now gather honey the greater portion be still cover every season with a repress growth of bee-flower for most of the species be annual and many of they be not relish by sheep or cattle while the rapidity of they growth enable they to develop and mature they seed before any foot have time to crush they the ground be therefore keep sweet and the race be perpetuate though only as a suggestive shadow of the magnificence of its wildness the time will undoubtedly come when the entire area of this noble valley will be till like a garden when the fertilize water of the mountain now flow to the sea will be distribute to every acre give rise to prosperous town wealth art etc then i suppose there will be few leave even among botanist to deplore the vanish primeval flora in the mean time the pure waste go on -- the wanton destruction of the innocent -- be a sad sight to see and the sun may well be pity in be compel to look california lilac these be the most important of all the honey-bearing bush of the sierra _ chamaebatium foliolosa _ a little shrub about a foot high with flower like the strawberry make handsome carpet beneath the pine and seem to be a favorite with the bee while pine themselves furnish unlimited quantity of pollen and honey-dew the product of a single tree ripen its pollen at the right time of year would be sufficient for the want of a whole hive along the stream there be a rich growth of lily larkspur pediculari castilleia and clover the alpine region contain the flowery glacier meadow and countless small garden in all sort of place full of potentillum of several species spraguea ivesium epilobium and goldenrod with bed of bryanthus and the charming cassiope cover with sweet bell dangerous height never come down again some undoubtedly perish in storm and i have find thousand lie dead or benumb on the surface of the glacier to which they have perhaps be attract by the white above sea-level at this height they flourish without care though the snow every winter be deep even higher than this several bee-tree have be cut which contain over 200 pound of honey the destructive action of sheep have not be so general on the mountain pasture as on those of the great plain but in many place it have be more complete owing to the more friable character of the soil and its sloping position the slant digging and down-raking action of hoof on the steeper slope of moraine have uproot and bury many of the tender plant from year to year without allow they time to mature they seed the shrub too be badly bite especially the various species of ceanothus fortunately neither sheep nor cattle care to feed on the manzanita spiraea or adenostoma and these fine honey-bush be too stiff and tall or grow in place too rough and inaccessible to be trodden under foot also the cañon wall and gorge which form so considerable a part of the area of the range while inaccessible to domestic sheep be well fringed with honey-shrub and contain thousand of lovely bee-garden lie hide in narrow side-cañons and recess fence with avalanche talus and on the top of flat project headland where only bee would think to look for they but on the other hand a great portion of the woody plant that escape the foot and tooth of the sheep be destroy by the shepherd by means of run fire which be set everywhere during the dry autumn for the purpose of burn off the old fall trunk and underbrush with a view to improve the pasture and make more open way for the flock these destructive sheep-fire sweep through nearly the entire forest belt of the range from one extremity to the other consume not only the underbrush but the young tree and seedling on which the permanence of the forest depend thus set in motion a long train of evil which will certainly reach far beyond bee and beekeeper -lrb- illustration : wild bee garden -rrb- the plow have not yet invade the forest region to any shasta be the most honeyful and may yet surpass in fame the celebrated honey hill of hyblum and hearthy hymettus regard this noble mountain from a bee point of view encircle by its many climate and sweeping aloft from the torrid plain into the frosty azure we find the first 5000 foot from the summit generally snow-clad and therefore about as honeyless as the sea the base of this arctic region be girdle by a belt of crumble lava measure about 1000 foot in vertical breadth and be mostly free from snow in summer beautiful lichen enliven the face of the cliff with they bright color and in some of the warmer nook there be a few tuft of alpine daisy wall-flower and pentstemon but notwithstanding these bloom freely in the late summer the zone as a whole be almost as honeyless as the icy summit and its lower edge may be take as the honey-line immediately below this come the forest zone cover with a rich growth of conifer chiefly silver fir rich in pollen and honey-dew and diversify with countless garden opening many of they less than a hundred yard across next in orderly succession come the great bee zone its area far surpass that of the icy summit and both the other zone combine for it go sweeping majestically around the entire mountain with a breadth of six or seven mile and a circumference of nearly a hundred mile shasta as we have already see be a fire-mountain create by a succession of eruption of ash and molten lava which flow over the lip of its several crater grow outward and upward like the trunk of a knotty exogenous tree then follow a strange contrast the glacial winter come on load the cooling mountain with ice which flow slowly outward in every direction radiate from the summit in the form of one vast conical glacier -- a down-crawling mantle of ice upon a fountain of smolder fire crush and grind for century its brown flinty lava with incessant activity and thus degrading and remodel the entire mountain when at length the glacial period begin to draw near its close the ice-mantle be gradually melt off around the bottom and in recede and break into its present fragmentary condition irregular ring and heap of moraine matter be store upon its flank the glacial erosion of most of the shasta lava produce detritus compose of rough sub-angular boulder of moderate size and of porous gravel and sand which yield freely to the transport power of run water magnificent flood from the ample fountain of ice and snow work with sublime energy upon this prepared glacial detritus sort it out and carry down immense quantity from the higher slope and reform it in smooth delta-like bed around the base and it be these flood-bed join together that now form the main honey-zone of the old volcano thus by force seemingly antagonistic and destructive have mother nature accomplish she beneficent design -- now a flood of fire now a flood of ice now a flood of water and at length a outburst of organic life a milky way of snowy petal and wing girdle the rugged mountain like a cloud as if the vivify sunbeam beat against its side have break into a foam of plant-bloom and bee as sea-wave break and bloom on a rock shore in this flowery wilderness the bee rove and revel rejoice in the bounty of the sun clamber eagerly through bramble and hucklebloom ring the myriad bell of the manzanita now hum aloft among polleny willow and fir now down on the ashy ground among gilia and buttercup and anon plunging deep into snowy bank of cherry and buckthorn they consider the lily and roll into they and like lily they toil not for they be impel by sun-power as water-wheel by water-power and when the one have plenty of high-pressure water the other plenty of sunshine they hum and quiver alike saunter in the shasta bee-land in the sun-day of summer one may readily infer the time of day from the comparative energy of bee-movement alone -- drowsy and moderate in the cool of the morning increase in energy with the ascend sun and at high noon thrilling and quiver in wild ecstasy then gradually decline again to the stillness of night in my excursion among the glacier i occasionally meet bee that be hungry like mountaineer who venture too far and remain too long above the bread-line then they droop and wither like autumn leave the shasta bee be perhaps better fed than any other in the sierra they field-work be one perpetual feast but however exhilarating the sunshine or bountiful the supply of flower they be always dainty feeder humming-moth and hummingbird seldom set foot upon a flower but poise on the wing in front of it and reach forward as if they be suck through straw but bee though as dainty as they hug they favorite flower with profound cordiality and push they blunt polleny face against they like baby on they mother 's bosom and fondly too with eternal love do mother nature clasp she small bee-baby and suckle they multitude at once on she warm shasta breast besides the common honey-bee there be many other species here -- fine mossy burly fellow who be nourish on the mountain thousand of sunny season before the advent of the domestic species among these be the bumblebee mason-bee carpenter-bee and leaf-cutter butterfly too and moth of every size and pattern some broad-winged like bat flap slowly and sailing in easy curve other like small fly violet shake about loosely in short crooked flight close to the flower feast luxuriously night and day great number of deer also delight to dwell in the brushy portion of the bee-pasture bear too roam the sweet wilderness they blunt shaggy form harmonize well with the tree and tangled bush and with the bee also notwithstanding the disparity in size they be fond of all good thing and enjoy they to the utmost with but little troublesome discrimination -- flower and leave as well as berry and the bee themselves as well as they honey though the californium bear have as yet have but little experience with honeybee they often succeed in reach they bountiful store and it seem doubtful whether bee themselves enjoy honey with so great a relish by means of they powerful tooth and claw they can gnaw and tear open almost any hive conveniently accessible most honey-bee however in search of a home be wise enough to make choice of a hollow in a living tree a considerable distance above the ground when such place be to be have then they be pretty secure for though the smaller black and brown bear climb well they be unable to break into strong hive while compel to exert themselves to keep from fall and at the same time to endure the sting of the fight bee effect of the drought be everywhere visible -- leafless field dead and die cattle dead bee and half-dead people with dusty doleful face even the bird and squirrel be in distress though they suffering above they or stand gorge on the ground beneath the tree wait with easy faith for fresh carcass the quail prudently consider the hard time abandon all thought of pairing they be too poor to marry and accustomed feeding-grounds betake themselves to the leafy oak to gnaw out the acorn store of the provident woodpecker but the latter keep up a vigilant watch upon they movement i notice four he be go to settle down he past life he say be of no account but the future be promising he be go to make money and marry a spanish woman people mine here for water as for gold he have be run a tunnel about half a hour 's walk above the cabin i come to the fall famous throughout the valley settlement as the finest yet discover in the san gabriel mountain it be a charming little thing with a low sweet voice singing like a bird as it pour from a notch in a short ledge some thirty-five or forty foot into a round mirror-pool the face of the cliff back of it and on both side be smoothly cover and wildness the last of a series extend down the flowery slope of mount san antonio through the rugged foam-beaten boss of the main eaton canon from the base of the fall i follow the ridge that form the most of the shasta chaparral be leafy nearly to the ground here the main stem be naked for three or four foot and interspike with dead twig form a stiff _ chevaux de frise _ through which even the bear make they way with difficulty i be compel to creep for mile on all fours and in follow the bear-trail often find tuft of hair on the bush where they have force themselves through for 100 foot or summit of the range it carry a bristly mane of chaparral here and there small opening occur on rocky place command fine view across the cultivate valley to the ocean these i find by the track be favorite outlook and resting-place for the wild animal -- bear wolf fox wildcat etc -- which abound here and would have to be take into account in the establishment of bee-ranch in the deepest thicket languid and wing-weary as if they have come all the way up from the flowerless valley after reach the summit i have time to make only a hasty survey of the basin now glowing in the sunset gold before the cañon be dry where i first reach it but a bunch of scarlet mimulus indicate water at no great distance and i soon discover about a bucketful in a hollow of the rock this however be full of dead
